<div id="review_358435953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358435953" />
    <a title="hpboy13" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6427364-hpboy13"><img alt="hpboy13" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395922187p2/6427364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358435953?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hpboy13" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hpboy13" href="/user/show/6427364-hpboy13">hpboy13</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6427364-hpboy13?shelf=hexalogy">hexalogy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358435953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15490774739473992505">The Warlock is definitely the low point of the "Secrets of the Immortal Series." I don't know why on earth Michael Scott deigned this with its own book, instead of consolidating it with The Enchantress and cutting out half the filler that's in both books. Both books take place over the course of one day, and this day at least is rather dull to read about. The climax of the book involves all the characters getting together for a BarBQ to read prophetic tablets about the upcoming finale. Yawn.<br/><br/>The </span>
  <span id="freeText15490774739473992505" style="display:none">The Warlock is definitely the low point of the "Secrets of the Immortal Series." I don't know why on earth Michael Scott deigned this with its own book, instead of consolidating it with The Enchantress and cutting out half the filler that's in both books. Both books take place over the course of one day, and this day at least is rather dull to read about. The climax of the book involves all the characters getting together for a BarBQ to read prophetic tablets about the upcoming finale. Yawn.<br /><br />The book does have its moments. In particular, the scenes with Machiavelli and Billy the Kid are the best in the book - a very interesting look at villains who have not lost their humanity. If only we could have had more of that.<br /><br />Also, this series suddenly seems to be going into a zillion bizarre directions. Suddenly, there's time-travel!! Um, what? Now there's political intrigue on Atlantis (or Danu Talis, as it's called)!! ...okay. If Scott wanted to write novels about political intrigue, he should have done that in a separate series, not tried to cram EVERYTHING into this bloated one.<br /><br />This series fell prey to every fantasy cliche that drives me nuts. There's a lot of Michael Scott trying waaaaay too hard to impress us. In the first two books, we established a hierarchy of immortals, Next Gen, Elder, and Great Elder. But Scott keeps trying to one-up himself - before the Great Elders were Archons, and before them Ancients, and before them Earthlords and blah blah blah. I'd really love it if he just decided on what the ultimate godlike race is and left it at that. There are also so many all-powerful mysterious figures creeping about - Marethyu, Tsagaglalal, etc - that it feels like overkill. And while on the subject, how about names that people can pronounce? There's a fine line between creativity and absurdity.<br /><br />If you've read the first foru books, then obviously you may as well finish the series, and there is a payoff in the end. I recommend reading this series, but I can't say it was one of my favorites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15490774739473992505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170759618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170759618" />
    <a title="Zephfire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2035830-zephfire"><img alt="Zephfire" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170759618?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zephfire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zephfire" href="/user/show/2035830-zephfire">Zephfire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170759618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6676752639847063657">If you haven't read the 4 titles in the 'Secrets of the Immortal Nicholas Flamel' series that come prior to The Warlock, then I would advise you do! Not only are you missing a great and award winning series, but the plot is very detailed and you may find it hard to follow the fast-paced roller coaster that this book is! <br/>My son and I have read all the prior titles and enjoyed them immensely, but this one is my favourite! <br/>The plot twists and turns at a break-neck pace, more characters are arriving</span>
  <span id="freeText6676752639847063657" style="display:none">If you haven't read the 4 titles in the 'Secrets of the Immortal Nicholas Flamel' series that come prior to The Warlock, then I would advise you do! Not only are you missing a great and award winning series, but the plot is very detailed and you may find it hard to follow the fast-paced roller coaster that this book is! <br />My son and I have read all the prior titles and enjoyed them immensely, but this one is my favourite! <br />The plot twists and turns at a break-neck pace, more characters are arriving, some we've met before, some are new to us, they have one of two aims.. to either aid Nicholas and Perenelle Flamel to retrieve the Codex and save the humani from certain suffering at the hands of the Dark Elders.. or to aid Dr Dee, Niccolo Machiavelli and the Dark Elders to gain the final two missing pages of the Codex and commence the Final Summoning that will see the humani enslaved to them as they regain control over the world. <br />Exactly who is on which side can never be guaranteed, and some characters are questioning the strength of their conviction and loyalty to their chosen side. <br />Josh Newman has left the Flamels and joined with Dr Dee.. will Sophie be able to convince him to return to the Flamels and to her side.. or will she leave the Flamels and her belief that they are doing the right thing, just to be re-united with her brother? <br />Meanwhile, some of the Flamel's supporters are off on a mission of their own, William Shakespeare, Comte de Saint-Germain, Scathach and Palamedes are in a very strange and mysterious place, having been taken there by the equally mysterious Marethyu.. who seems to have an agenda all of his own, but which side of this epic battle is he on? <br />You'll need to read The Warlock to find out the answers.. and it's an exciting, spellbinding and totally absorbing read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6676752639847063657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_244210271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Սամուէլ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3633989"><img alt="Սամուէլ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552074453p2/3633989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/244210271?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Սամուէլ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Սամուէլ" href="/user/show/3633989">Սամուէլ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3633989?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3633989?shelf=mythological-fiction">mythological-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer244210271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17835797058841822437">Scott's <i>The Warlock</i> was an interesting read. I'm a little conflicted over how I feel about it though. Did it include new mythological/historical characters that made me jump to wikipedia to learn more? Yes. Did the plot undergo significant development? Yes. Did any of my predictions come true? No. So did it live up to my expectations? I'm not sure. <br/> Don't misinterpret what I'm saying, I love Scott's writing and his series, but something felt missing from this specific book. After waiting for ove</span>
  <span id="freeText17835797058841822437" style="display:none">Scott's <i>The Warlock</i> was an interesting read. I'm a little conflicted over how I feel about it though. Did it include new mythological/historical characters that made me jump to wikipedia to learn more? Yes. Did the plot undergo significant development? Yes. Did any of my predictions come true? No. So did it live up to my expectations? I'm not sure. <br /> Don't misinterpret what I'm saying, I love Scott's writing and his series, but something felt missing from this specific book. After waiting for over a year to get my hands on it, the book took me <i>two months</i> to read. Something just seams wrong about that. The characters and their interactions were amazing, and I loved learning about the island of Danu Talis, but I kept getting distracted from the story. <br /> Regardless, I'd still recommend this book to anyone (who's read the first four books of the series) because the ending was <b>amazing</b> and I can't get it out of my head. I had absolutely no clue that Scott would reveal something so extreme in the last line of the entire book. I felt all the excitement of the series return at the end, and am now desperately waiting for <i>The Enchantress</i> to come out and conclude the series. If you're interested in these books, or are considering reading them, do so. You won't regret it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17835797058841822437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-nelson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338604922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2495519187512771197">I can’t believe this series is almost done, and yet, WOW! Be prepared for some intense reveals throughout this book, and definitely have The Enchantress ready to read after you finish it, because you’re going to want to read it right away.<br/><br/>Overall, I’ve really enjoyed the progression of The Secrets of the Immortal Nicolas Flamel. It gets better and better as it focuses more on the twins and their lives and goes away from Nicolas Flamel himself. In this book, we see so much more of Danu Talis, whi</span>
  <span id="freeText2495519187512771197" style="display:none">I can’t believe this series is almost done, and yet, WOW! Be prepared for some intense reveals throughout this book, and definitely have The Enchantress ready to read after you finish it, because you’re going to want to read it right away.<br /><br />Overall, I’ve really enjoyed the progression of The Secrets of the Immortal Nicolas Flamel. It gets better and better as it focuses more on the twins and their lives and goes away from Nicolas Flamel himself. In this book, we see so much more of Danu Talis, which was probably my favorite part of the whole book. I love how everything is coming together and all the parts are falling into place. While it still keeps up the action, not much actually happens in this book. It’s mostly the result of some plots falling into place while setting up for the finale, The Enchantress. With that said, this book is highly entertaining and I loved getting to know more about various characters. I’m also just so ready for Sophie and Josh to stop being estranged at this point. We’ll see if that happens, though.<br /><br />It’s hard to say much of anything without ruining things. It’s fun and it’s still going strong. I would still highly recommend this series!<br /><br />Also posted on <a href="http://www.purplereaders.com/?p=5349" rel="nofollow noopener">Purple People Readers</a>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12156386393682330570">I felt like this series started well but is now very chaotic. What seemed like a JK Rowling-Rick Riordan baby has turned into a Riordan-Lewis Carroll baby. Mythology on acid. Ever had the kind of dream where you're on Alcatraz and you've cracked an egg in your hand but you don't let go? And a 7-headed baby dragon is now drinking your blood from your hand because you're its new mommy? But your friend thinks it's dangerous so she tries to knock it out of your hand and lull it to sleep with her mag</span>
  <span id="freeText12156386393682330570" style="display:none">I felt like this series started well but is now very chaotic. What seemed like a JK Rowling-Rick Riordan baby has turned into a Riordan-Lewis Carroll baby. Mythology on acid. Ever had the kind of dream where you're on Alcatraz and you've cracked an egg in your hand but you don't let go? And a 7-headed baby dragon is now drinking your blood from your hand because you're its new mommy? But your friend thinks it's dangerous so she tries to knock it out of your hand and lull it to sleep with her magical wooden flute? But you triumphantly tell your friend that the creature is deaf, hahaha! So you put the creature in the ocean and it grows like one those dehydrated spongy things on TV, and then it goes and tries to destroy San Francisco, but that's what you wanted it to do all along? You think it makes sense, but you wake up and you're so confused by how insane it is? Yeah, I just summarized a whole chapter of this book. My advice is read the first book and stop.</span>

    <a title="Jeffrey P" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4141052-jeffrey-p"><img alt="Jeffrey P" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174860732" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16087068506358087801">I guess the best I can say about The Warlock is that it's (much) better than The Necromancer. However, the formula is getting a bit tired at this point: Josh and Sophie visit a different city, mythological monsters and immortals appear, stuff gets blown up, and most of them survive to live another day (and book). I am desperate for the last book to appear, not because I need to read the finale, but because this series will finally be over. A classic case of a one or two book story lengthened int</span>
  <span id="freeText16087068506358087801" style="display:none">I guess the best I can say about The Warlock is that it's (much) better than The Necromancer. However, the formula is getting a bit tired at this point: Josh and Sophie visit a different city, mythological monsters and immortals appear, stuff gets blown up, and most of them survive to live another day (and book). I am desperate for the last book to appear, not because I need to read the finale, but because this series will finally be over. A classic case of a one or two book story lengthened into an epic. <br /><br />That all said, what I do like about the series is the greyness of good-and-evil; in the Alchemist we think that Nicolas and Perenelle are good guys, come to save the world and that Dee and his companions are bad. Now we realize that Dee is bad (in fact, he's *really* bad) but it's not so clear that Nicolas and Perenelle are the white knights we originally assumed.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('W4c0H9GgO7b4jZJjgQYlceVBGnW5zmDfMtSj6LOmXzbVOeD/7ZcSBpaVQgADqocbPbP5TdNmFzvnVuKwn7Ithw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7lKqOq6AkHpVIG0MPGgQHuiZh/IbAKp9oyMrWvwhkD9g7H7akre5yjs4vW++xLJ0MGtkynGo3Zl2oWoC0DXijg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer3035579550581146657">Irish-born Michael Scott began writing over thirty years ago, and is one of Ireland's most successful and prolific authors, with over one hundred titles to his credit, spanning a<br/>variety of genres, including Fantasy, Science Fiction and Folklore. <br/><br/>He writes for both adults and young adults and is published in thirty-seven countries, in over twenty languages.<br/><br/>Praised for his “unparalleled contribution</span>
  <span id="freeText3035579550581146657" style="display:none">Irish-born Michael Scott began writing over thirty years ago, and is one of Ireland's most successful and prolific authors, with over one hundred titles to his credit, spanning a<br />variety of genres, including Fantasy, Science Fiction and Folklore. <br /><br />He writes for both adults and young adults and is published in thirty-seven countries, in over twenty languages.<br /><br />Praised for his “unparalleled contribution to children’s literature,” by the Guide to Children’s<br />Books, Michael Scott was the Writer in Residence during Dublin’s tenure as European City of Culture in 1991, and was featured in the 2006 edition of Who’s Who in Ireland as one of the 1000<br />most “significant Irish.”<br /></span>
